### 2026-06-19 — Guide_17 Player Shops: authoritative quality pass — phantom `bargain` command killed, buy/sell/order syntax corrected, 10% haggle cap, up-front escrow, relist fee, in-place upgrade (Opus loop) — *drop guide-17-player-shops*
Opus-owned GUIDES quality pass over **Guide_17 Player Shops & Trading** (the passive-revenue commerce guide), cross-checked against `engine/vendor_droids.py`, `engine/skill_checks.resolve_bargain_check`, `parser/shop_commands.py`, the customer `buy`/`sell` routers (`parser/space_commands.py` / `parser/builtin_commands.py`) and `data/vendor_droids.yaml`. The guide carried a cluster of test-INVISIBLE command-surface and mechanical drift (the convention invariant guards the registry, not guide prose):
- **PHANTOM `bargain` command killed.** §1/§4/§5/§13 taught `bargain <slot>` as a customer move. There is no `bargain` command at all — the haggle is applied AUTOMATICALLY inside the customer's `buy`, and only on Tier 2+ droids (`buy_from_droid` runs the Bargain check only `if b_dice > 0 or b_pips > 0`). A **Tier 1 droid never haggles** — it sells at the listed price (the guide previously claimed the opposite: that Tier 1 "customers can always haggle prices down").
- **Haggle cap corrected 10-25% → 10%.** `resolve_bargain_check` maps ±2% per 4 points of opposed-roll margin, capped ±10%. The "10-25% off" prose was wrong.
- **Customer buy syntax** `buy <slot> [quantity]` → **`buy <slot#> from <shop name>`** (or item name); `buy_from_droid` has NO quantity param (one unit per buy).
- **Buy-order fulfilment** `sell <qty> to <shop>` → **`sell <resource> to <shop name>`** (resource name; quantity automatic, up to the order's remaining need).
- **Posting a buy order** `shop order <item> <max_price> [qty]` → **`shop order <resource> <min_quality> <qty> <price_per>`** (four args, crafting-resources only). The old `shop order metal 50 100` example would not even parse.
- **Buy orders are resource-only** (validated vs crafting `RESOURCE_TYPES`) — not "buy completed items from other crafters"; **escrow is deducted up front** at post time (full `qty × price_per`), not gradually as customers sell; the **phantom "max 5 simultaneous orders" cap removed** (no count cap exists — escrow is the limiter). Cancelling refunds unspent escrow.
- **Tier upgrade** is `shop upgrade <tier>` IN PLACE (inventory preserved, price difference charged: gn4→gn7 3,000 / gn7→gn12 7,000 / gn4→gn12 10,000 cr) — §1's "buy a new droid, transfer inventory, sell the old one back for a refund" was phantom (no droid-sellback mechanism exists).
- **Documented the live but previously-omitted recurring relisting fee** (1% of slot value, min 10 cr, on listings idle >30 days, daily `vendor_relist_fee` sink) in §4/§9/§14.
- VERIFIED ACCURATE vs HEAD (now pinned): tier costs/slots/fees/bargain pools (`data/vendor_droids.yaml`), 50% price floor (`PRICE_FLOOR_PCT`), 30/60-day warn/recall (`_WARN_DAYS`/`_RECALL_DAYS`), 2/room + 3/owner droid caps, the four forbidden room types + `no_commerce`, `market search [planet|all]` (bare `market` = cargo prices).
- `tests/test_guide_17_player_shops.py` (32) resolves every taught command against the live registry, asserts `bargain` is NOT a command, and pins every number against the engine constants. Docs/test only; engine + data READ-ONLY; era-clean; no schema, no faucet/sink.
- **FLAGGED follow-up (engine, NOT done — possible balance bug):** the `if b_dice > 0 or b_pips > 0` gate means a **Tier 1 droid never engages the haggle**, so it sells at full sticker — likely the *opposite* of the intended "Tier 1 is easy to haggle down, upgrade to protect prices" design. If intended behavior is that Tier 1 has a weak/zero pool customers easily beat (rather than no haggle at all), the gate should let Tier 1 through `resolve_bargain_check` (which floors the NPC pool at 1D). Guide now documents HEAD's actual behavior; left engine untouched (guides are docs-only). Worth a Brian ruling.

The Opus-owned guides quality pass over the Security Zones guide (the EVE-style Secured/Contested/Lawless layer that gates all combat). Verified every command the guide teaches against the SAME live registry `server/game_server` builds and cross-checked every quantified mechanic against the live engine. **Phantom removed:** §6 + §9 promised a **"+25% CP tick-rate bonus while in a lawless zone"** — no such modifier exists. `engine/cp_engine` has exactly four income sources (passive trickle / scene bonus / kudos / AI evaluator) and is entirely zone-blind; standing in a lawless room earns no CP at all. Rewrote both passages to state CP accrues from *play* (missions, scenes, kudos) — which dangerous zones host more of — not from loitering. **Command-reference fixes (test-invisible — the convention-invariant test guards the registry, not guide prose):** §8 mischaracterized `@security override <room> = none` as a generic "clear any override" and omitted the actual `@security override <room> = <faction>` **set form** — the `override` subform is a per-room *faction override* (hostile/unfriendly PCs of the named faction see a SECURED room as LAWLESS), not a security-level toggle. Rewrote §8 to teach all four real subforms and the persistence model (admin `@security` zone-sets write the DB → durable; Director surges/crackdowns are in-memory → reset on restart). §7 still described the **retired per-room** claim model; corrected to the live **per-region** wilderness ownership (`faction claim`; LAWLESS→CONTESTED citadel upgrade for the owning org's members; non-members and independents see base; ceiling is CONTESTED, never SECURED). **Completeness (Opus depth pass):** §2 expanded from "four things" to the full resolution set — added the **room faction-override** (#5) and **player-city citizen upgrade** (#6, CONTESTED→SECURED / LAWLESS→CONTESTED for citizens) factors the engine actually applies in `_finalize`; §3 now documents the **`+pvp` self-flag** (open PvP in CONTESTED only, never overrides SECURED, 5-minute anti-tag-and-flee cooldown) the guide previously omitted; §6 softened the "rare resources ONLY in lawless" overstatement (Contested/Control rooms also carry a T5-rare chance per the harvest yield table). **Mechanics verified accurate against HEAD (now pinned):** §3 challenge TTL = `_PVP_CHALLENGE_TTL` 600s (10 min) + `+pvp` unflag = `PVP_UNFLAG_COOLDOWN_S` 300s (5 min); §2 influence thresholds (underworld ≥80 downgrade / authority ≥75 upgrade / authority ≥90 martial-law forced-SECURED) match `_apply_director_overlay` behaviorally; §5 space-tier mapping (DOCK→secured, ORBIT/HYPERSPACE→contested, DEEP_SPACE→lawless) matches `_SPACE_SECURITY_BY_TYPE`; §7 citadel upgrade matches `_apply_wilderness_ownership`; §4 `+bounty/claim` resolves (umbrella `+bounty`, switch `claim`). New `tests/test_guide_04_security_zones.py` (27): every taught command resolves, the phantom stays dead (no `+25%` in the guide + `cp_engine` asserted zone-blind), and each numeric claim is cross-checked against the engine so a future retune that desyncs the guide fails loudly. Docs/content + test only; no engine logic, no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `security.py`/`cp_engine.py`/`combat_commands.py`/`harvest.py` read-only (avoid-lane untouched).

### 2026-06-19 — SpaceGrid boot rehydration (LOW verify finding — ships visible after restart) — *drop spacegrid-boot-rehydration*
Fixes the LOW finding from `VERIFY_FINDINGS_2026-06-18.md`: after a server restart, the in-memory `SpaceGrid` was rebuilt empty — undocked, realspace ships were absent from the combat/range/targeting grid until each pilot explicitly relaunched, meaning any session that began shortly after a restart had broken targeting and combat-range for ships that were already in space. Fix: `game_server.start()` now queries `db.get_ships_in_space()` (non-docked rows) immediately before starting the network listeners, filters out ships in hyperspace (correctly absent until `hyperspace_arrival_tick` re-adds them on exit), and calls `self.space_grid.add_ship()` for each realspace ship, mirroring the exact pattern used by `hyperspace_arrival_tick`. Per-ship JSON parse is guarded (`try/except JSONDecodeError`) so one malformed systems blob can't abort the whole rehydration block; the outer try/except makes the whole step fail-open (log warning, game boots). New `tests/test_spacegrid_boot_rehydration.py` (10 tests): basic add-ship/empty-grid, realspace ship added at correct speed, hyperspace ship skipped, mixed fleet, unknown-template fallback speed (5), empty ship list, malformed JSON gracefully treated as empty dict, hyperspace-arrival add-ship non-regression, get_ships_in_space drift guard (SQL must exclude `docked_at IS NULL`). Server/game-server only; no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean, no avoid-lane. (Sonnet loop)

### 2026-06-19 — Guide_03 Ground Combat: authoritative quality pass (2 broken combat-command references fixed + engine cross-check guard) (Opus loop) — *drop guide-03-ground-combat*
The Opus-owned guides quality pass over the largest, most-played guide (Ground Combat, 38 KB). Verified **every** combat command the guide teaches against the SAME live registry `server/game_server` builds, and cross-checked the §4/§5/§7/§9/§11/§14 mechanics tables against the live engine constants. **Two test-INVISIBLE broken command references fixed** (the convention-invariant test guards the registry, not free-text guide prose, so the unit suite couldn't see these): **(1) §13 posing** taught `> pose <text>` to submit a combat pose — but bare `pose` is the generic room-emote alias (`EmoteCommand` key `emote`, aliases `:`/`pose`/`em`); it broadcasts an ordinary emote and never registers as the round's combat pose, silently leaving the player with the auto-pose. Fixed to the real command **`cpose <text>`** (`CombatPoseCommand`, alias `combatpose`), with an explicit teaching note distinguishing it from the bare `pose`/`:` emote. **(2) §16 quick reference** listed `force-point` (hyphenated) — the registered key is `forcepoint` (aliases `fp`/`+fp`), no hyphenated alias exists, so `force-point` resolved to nothing; fixed to `forcepoint` (or `fp`). Also added the missing `cpose` quick-ref row, aligned the `crolls`/`combat rolls` and `cover [quarter|half|3/4|full]` rows to the engine's actual vocabulary. **Mechanics verified accurate against HEAD (no change needed, now pinned):** §5 damage-margin → wound bands (1–3 Stunned / 4–8 Wounded / 9–12 Incapacitated / 13–15 Mortally Wounded / 16+ Dead) match `WoundLevel.from_damage_margin` at every boundary; §4/§7 cover dice (+1D/+2D/+3D for 1/4·1/2·3/4) match `COVER_QUARTER`/`COVER_HALF`/`COVER_THREE_QUARTER`; §9 aim cap (+3D) matches `min(actor.aim_bonus + 1, 3)`; §11 NPC-AI table lists exactly the five live `CombatBehavior` profiles (aggressive/defensive/cowardly/berserk/sniper); §14 mortal-wound death roll (2D, die if total < rounds mortally wounded) matches `engine/combat.py`. New `tests/test_guide_03_ground_combat.py` (29): every taught command resolves, both fixes pinned (no `force-point`, no bare `> pose` instruction, `cpose` taught), and each mechanics table cross-checked against the engine so a future retune that desyncs the guide fails loudly. Docs/content + test only; no engine logic, no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; combat.py/character.py/npc_combat_ai.py read-only (avoid-lane untouched).

### 2026-06-19 — QA L3 remainder: stale `cp_commands` doubling claim removed + guard test (Sonnet loop) — *drop l3-cp-docstring*
**QA L3 (QA_FINDINGS_2026-06-16.md)** found that `advance_skill()` contained a dead if-branch and a docstring claiming "cost doubled above attribute" — but the code never doubles (WEG R&E rule: cost = current total dice, period). The `advance_skill` fix + tests landed earlier (the source no longer says "doubled", the dead branch is gone). This drop closes the **remaining L3 artifact**: the `parser/cp_commands.py` **module docstring** at line 15 still said `"train costs current_dice CP (doubled if above attribute)"` — wrong, and unchecked by the existing L3 tests (which scope to `Character.advance_skill`). Fixed to `"train costs total_dice CP (WEG R&E rule: current total dice, no doubling)"`. New guard: `TestL3CpCommandsDocstring.test_no_doubled_claim_in_module_docstring` (1 test, added to `tests/test_qa_m4_l3_planet_achievement.py`) — checks the `parser.cp_commands` module docstring for the "doubled" claim so this can't regress silently. Comment-only fix; no engine logic, no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean, no avoid-lane touched.

### 2026-06-19 — In-game `Type 'X'` command hints: post-rework breakage sweep + durable guard (Opus loop) — *drop ingame-hint-resolve*
The command-syntax rework (Drops 0-7) deleted the bare query/meta forms and made the `+`-prefixed variant canonical. The guide-syntax guards swept player-facing **guide prose**, but the dozens of imperative `Type 'X'` hints emitted from **engine/parser code in live play** were an unguarded surface — a hint that tells a new player to `Type 'missions'` when the bare form was deleted is a "command not found" the unit suite can't see (the convention-invariant test guards the registry, not free-text hint strings). Audited every `Type 'X'` hint in `engine/`/`parser/`/`server/` against the SAME live registry `server/game_server` builds (resolving the base word through aliases + `+cmd/<switch>` bases). Of 30+ hints, the bulk resolve fine (`help`/`?`/`commands` are sanctioned `+help` aliases the rework kept; bare combat verbs `attack`/`dodge`/`aim`/`flee`/`cover`/`range` are registered at their bare keys; `missions`/`bounties`/`powers`/`weapons`/etc. resolve via alias). **Two were genuinely broken and are fixed:** (1) **`engine/spacer_quest.py`** step-8 hint `Type 'factions'` → `Type '+factions'` — bare `factions` was deleted by the rework, so every new spacer following the sector-intel hint hit a dead command. (2) **`parser/space_commands.py`** `@spawn` unknown-template error pointed admins at a nonexistent `Type 'ships'` command → now lists the real available template keys from the in-process registry (`", ".join(sorted(t.key for t in reg.all_templates()))`), non-phantom discovery using the existing `ShipRegistry.all_templates()` API. **Documented non-breakages:** `boarding_link`/`boarding_link_back` are movement EXITS (`engine/boarding.py` `BOARDING_EXIT_DIR_TO`/`_FROM`), resolved by the movement system not the command registry — you cross a boarding link by typing the exit name like `north`; allowlisted. **Tech-debt flagged:** `engine/tutorial.py` (v1 `TutorialManager`) is instantiated at `game_server.py:454` but **never driven** (no `start`/`advance`/`skip` call site anywhere) — superseded by the chain-tutorial system selected at chargen; its `Type 'skip tutorial'` hints are unreachable dead code (the real `training skip` is itself disabled). Excluded from the guard pending removal (`TODO.json` `tech_debt.tutorial_v1_dead_code`). New `tests/test_ingame_command_hints_resolve.py` (4): every live `Type 'X'` hint resolves against the registry (caught **2 additional** would-be false-positive data-type docstrings — `objects` rows `of type 'breachable'` — excluded by a precise regex), allowlist entries are genuinely not commands, + regression pins on both fixes. Chargen-internal hints (`creation.py`/`creation_wizard.py` free-form loop) are excluded — that vocabulary is its own input loop, guarded separately. String/docs + test only; no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; no avoid-lane file touched.

### 2026-06-19 — Verify-campaign MEDIUM fixes: rate-bucket address-reuse + IP-throttle empty-key leak — *drop verify-fixes-mem-leaks*
Three memory/correctness fixes from `VERIFY_FINDINGS_2026-06-18.md` MEDIUM findings (Sonnet loop). **(1) Parser rate-bucket address-reuse fix (`parser/commands.py`).** `CommandParser._check_rate_limit` keyed its per-session token bucket on `id(session)` — the CPython memory address, which is reused after GC. A new session created at the same address inherited the previous session's drained bucket, causing cross-session rate-limit bleed (new players briefly unable to type fast). Fixed: key on `session.id` (monotonically increasing `Session._next_id`, never reused). Added `CommandParser.clear_session(session_id)` to remove the stale entry on disconnect. Wired the cleanup into `GameServer` at all three session-removal sites (kicked-existing on token-auth, kicked-existing on password-auth, and normal session teardown). **(2) IP-throttle empty-key leak (`server/api.py`).** `_sliding_window_allow` used `bucket[ip]` (defaultdict — creates the key on first access) and never deleted the key when pruning left it empty. Over time every distinct IP that ever hit a throttled endpoint accumulated a stale empty-list key. Fixed: use `bucket.get(ip, [])` instead (no phantom key creation) and `bucket.pop(ip, None)` when pruning leaves the list empty. This fix covers all three throttle dicts that route through `_sliding_window_allow`: the strict chargen-write limiter (`_rate_limits`), the soft read-endpoint limiter (`_soft_rate_limits`), and the pre-auth connect/create limiter (`_preauth_attempts` in `game_server.py`, which imports this function). **(3) Portal login-throttle empty-key leak (`server/web_portal.py`).** `_login_rate_ok` had the same inline pattern. Fixed to match. New `tests/test_verify_mem_leaks.py` (12 tests): key-delete-on-expiry, no-phantom-key-on-first-get, rate-limit-at-max (sliding window), login-rate cleanup, CommandParser keyed-on-session-id not address, clear_session no-op for unknown id. No schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean, no avoid-lane.

---

### The faithfulness crux — `resolve_natural_attack`
**13 of 14** creatures carry a natural attack stronger than bare STR, recorded as WEG prose: relative (`STR+1D`, `STR+2D+2`, `STR+2`), absolute (`1D`), or specials (`Poison 5D`, grapple `opposed (..)`, `+3D/round`). The combat engine's unarmed path only knew bare STR, so spawning raw would halve their danger. The new resolver parses the clean `STR(+ND)(+N)` / `ND(+N)` forms into a concrete dice string via `DicePool` (pips normalize: magus `STR 1D+1 + "STR+2"` → **2D**; stalker `STR 3D + "STR+2D+2"` → **5D+2**; voroos `STR 6D + "STR+1D, then grasp"` → **7D** + special flag), and **falls back to bare STR** for poison/grapple/multi-round riders while flagging `special` so the spawn flavor still carries the rider. Full poison/grapple *mechanics* are a documented follow-up.

### Pieces
- **`engine/creature_library.py`** (new, PURE): `load_creature_library` (cached), `get_creature`, `resolve_natural_attack`, `build_creature_char_sheet`, `build_creature_ai_config`, `creature_spawn_count`.
- **`engine/character.py`** + **`engine/npc_combat_ai.py`** (minimal combat-path change): `Character` gains `natural_attack_skill`/`natural_attack_damage`, set in `from_npc_sheet` from the char_sheet's `natural_attack` marker; `_get_npc_weapon` honors it **first** (returns `(brawling, resolved_damage, "")`) before the equipped-weapon / bare-STR fallback. Ordinary NPCs are unaffected (fields default empty — explicitly tested).
- **`engine/wilderness_encounter_runtime.py`** (new, IO): `spawn_encounter_creatures` (loads creature, builds faithful sheet+ai, `db.create_npc` × count) + `_start_encounter_combat` (mirrors `dsp_hunter_runtime._start_hunter_combat`) + `resolve_encounter_spawn` orchestrator.
- **`parser/builtin_commands.py`** (~1316): guarded wire after the encounter narrative — a `hostile`/`non_hostile` encounter with a resolvable `npc_template` spawns the creature(s); a `hostile` one starts combat immediately.

### Tests / verification
`tests/test_lane_a_phase_b_spawner.py` (+18) against the real resolver/builders, the real `Character` + `_get_npc_weapon`, and the bridge spawn-logic via a fake db (asserts N creates with the faithful `5D+2` sheet, hostile flag, numbered names, and no-spawn for weather/anomaly/no-template/unknown). 18/18 green; the 3 existing Lane A suites still green; combat/character sandbox tests unaffected.

- **Deferred (documented):** special-attack mechanics (poison/grapple/swallow beyond base damage); remaining biomes (Kamino/Geonosis still region-less, Kuat miner's-horror is starfighter-scale → space path); creature-harvest sinks (still no runtime path).
- **Pending you:** full Windows suite + a live smoke — wander a region until a hostile creature encounter fires, confirm the creature spawns and combat starts (e.g. a stalker lizard hits for ~`5D+2`, not `3D`).
- **Handoff:** `HANDOFF_lane_a_phase_b_spawner_2026-06-05.md`.

- **Files:** `engine/creature_library.py` (new), `engine/wilderness_encounter_runtime.py` (new), `engine/character.py`, `engine/npc_combat_ai.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `tests/test_lane_a_phase_b_spawner.py` (new).

## 2026-06-05 — village_trials dark-future-self re-key + clone_wars data era-sweep (T2.CW.codebase_era_sweep)

Two era-cleanness items, rolled into the cumulative zip. Asked to judge whether the village Trial-of-Spirit's dark-future-self (which shows Imperial/Rebel imagery) is a coherent dramatic moment or a cleanup miss — verdict: **both**. The concept is a coherent, canonically-apt Force-vision of the dark age to come (the one sanctioned B3 exception — the Imperial variant says *"you will be told the Empire does not exist yet"* in-fiction), but the **wiring** was a cleanup miss.

### village_trials.py — re-key to CW factions (the prophecy was unreachable dead code)
`_SPIRIT_TURNS_BY_FACTION` and `_COURAGE_TEMPLATES_BY_FACTION` were keyed on dead GCW faction names (`separatist`/`imperial`/`rebel`) that **no CW character carries** (CW factions are `republic`/`cis`/`jedi_order`/`hutt_cartel`/`bounty_hunters_guild`/`independent`), so the gorgeous Imperial and Rebel future-visions were a write-with-no-reader. Re-keyed both registries to route present allegiance → canonical future, with **zero content loss**:

- **Spirit:** `republic`→Imperial (the GAR→Empire arc, ~1yr to Order 66), `cis`→Separatist, `jedi_order`→the Republic war-machine vision (*"the Order will use you"*), `hutt_cartel`+`bounty_hunters_guild`→Cartel, `independent`→Rebellion. Every variant now reachable; the redundant aged-GAR vision found its home on `jedi_order` rather than being retired.
- **Courage** (era-neutral recitals): `separatist`→`cis`; the orphaned `imperial` text (*"the order said don't"* — a Jedi double meaning) →`jedi_order`; the orphaned `rebel` text (*"the cause"*) →`independent`.

Added a documenting comment marking the dark-future-self as the deliberate B3 prophecy exception. Guard/reachability tests in `tests/test_f7c4_village_spirit.py` and `tests/test_f7c2_village_courage.py` (re-pointed to CW factions + new `no-dead-GCW-keys` assertions). These files are pytest-style (Windows-only); validated in-sandbox by direct invocation of the composers across all six CW factions.

### clone_wars data slice — three player-facing leaks fixed
- `zones.yaml` (Geonosis Petranaki) — *"the original Death Star plans"* → *"the original superweapon schematics"*. The Geonosian-superweapon reference is era-accurate deep canon (~22 BBY) and is kept; only the anachronistic proper noun is removed.
- `tutorials/rooms.yaml` (Smugglers' Alley) — a leaked *"Imperial — well, Republic"* slip a 20 BBY vendor couldn't make, cut to *"Republic patrols"*.
- `planets/coruscant.yaml` (Opera House `short_desc`) — *"Imperial City"* (the GCW name) → *"Galactic City"*.

Left untouched (legitimate): era-mapping keys (`imperial: republic`), `replaces:` rewicker metadata, "no Empire" disclaimers in comments, and lowercase "rebellion" (= the CIS secession). Guard: `tests/test_e3_data_era_cleanness.py` (scans player-facing string values in the three files; +5). `validate_world` = 0 errors. The design-call queue is now empty.

- **Files:** `engine/village_trials.py`; `data/worlds/clone_wars/zones.yaml`; `data/worlds/clone_wars/tutorials/rooms.yaml`; `data/worlds/clone_wars/planets/coruscant.yaml`; `tests/test_f7c4_village_spirit.py`; `tests/test_f7c2_village_courage.py`; `tests/test_e3_data_era_cleanness.py` (**new**).

## 2026-06-05 — Morale-skill broadening (T2.11.b) + Coruscant §3 re-zoning (T2.5), both fully implemented

Brian delegated both design calls ("use your judgment; I always want the complete, fully implemented choice"). Rolled into the cumulative zip.

### T2.11.b — morale-flavored skill set
Broadened `MORALE_FLAVORED_SKILLS` (engine/skill_checks.py) from the v1 four to the cantina-social core: **+bargain** (haggling buoyed by good cheer), **+gambling** (confidence at the sabacc table — the cantina's heart), **+streetwise** (working a lively room for information). **Intimidation deliberately excluded** — the aura *uplifts* mood, while intimidation instills *fear*; a warm, lively room makes it harder, not easier. Combat/technical/mechanical/knowledge/Force-power rolls remain unaffected.

### T2.5 — Coruscant security-zone naming → §3 function taxonomy
Migrated all 8 Coruscant vertical-tier zones to the `security_model_design_v1.md` §3.1 function districts, and reconciled the **three** security schemes that had drifted apart (zones.yaml `properties.security` — the canonical one read by `security.py`; coruscant.yaml per-room `security_level:`; and the hardcoded `_ZONE_SECURITY` dict in `engine/housing_lots_provider.py`) to the §3 tiers.

| Old zone | → §3 zone | §3 security |
|---|---|---|
| coruscant_senate | senate_district | Secured |
| coruscant_temple | jedi_temple | Secured |
| coruscant_upper | monumental_district | Secured |
| coruscant_midlevels | commercial_district | Secured |
| coruscant_works | commercial_district (**merged**) | Secured |
| coruscant_gilded_cage | entertainment_district | Secured |
| coruscant_lower | southern_underground | **Contested** |
| coruscant_underworld | coruscant_underworld | Lawless |

**Judgment calls made:** (1) the Works folds into `commercial_district` (Secured) rather than becoming its own zone — §3 mandates exactly one contested hand-built zone, and the Works is CSF-patrolled infrastructure; (2) `southern_underground` is that single Contested hand-built zone (the Cantina-Sanctuary archetype). The Temple already had its own zone, so the §3 `jedi_temple` carve-out was a rename, not a new cut.

**Scope:** the rename swept 32 files + `zones.yaml` keys + the `npcs_drop_c2` roster file (renamed on disk `coruscant_lower` → `southern_underground`). Because room slugs were zone-prefixed, the sweep also renamed room slugs (e.g., `coruscant_works_landing_zone` → `commercial_district_landing_zone`) consistently across coruscant.yaml, chains.yaml, and code — `validate_world` reports **0 errors**, all **72/72 room slugs unique** (the works→commercial merge created no collisions), and there are no leftover old refs. Per-room `security_level` is now 27 secured / 13 contested / 1 lawless (was a pre-§3 21/13/7). Guard test: `tests/test_t2_5_and_t2_11b_morale_and_rezone.py` (+11; also re-greened `test_drop_c2_coruscant` and `test_f8c2b_chain_events` after the rename).

## 2026-06-05 — Drop 4b hunter.2: live-spawn climax + reward-on-defeat (rolled in with the decision-clearing drop)

- **Wave:** Drop 4b (Dark-Side roaming hunter). hunter.1 (the deterministic pursuit tracker) shipped earlier this session; this is hunter.2-A.
- **Files:** `engine/dsp_hunter.py` (pure additions); `engine/dsp_hunter_runtime.py` (**new**, IO orchestration); `db/database.py` (SCHEMA_VERSION 41→42 + `MIGRATIONS[42]` + `set_dsp_pursuit_spawn`); `server/tick_handlers_progression.py` (`dsp_hunter_tick` spawn/reconcile/despawn); `parser/combat_commands.py` (combat-death hook); `tests/test_hunter2_spawn_reward.py` (**new**).
- **Tests:** +11 (`tests/test_hunter2_spawn_reward.py`); hunter.1 pure-module suite still green (the one DB-touching test in `test_drop4b_dsp_hunter` errors only on the sandbox's missing `aiosqlite` — environmental, passes on Windows).
- **What it shipped — the climax.** When a Dark-Side pursuit reaches `at_heels` and the quarry is online, a **real, fightable hunter NPC** is now spawned into their room and the fight **auto-starts**. The hunter's stats scale to the quarry's DSP tier (Marked/Hunted/Darkest → blaster 5D/6D/7D, tougher dodge/attributes), built by the pure `hunter_combat_sheet`/`hunter_ai_config` and dropped in via `db.create_npc`. The spawn reuses the same ctx-free combat primitives `engine/encounter_boarding.py` uses (`_get_or_create_combat`/`_broadcast_events`/`_auto_declare_npc_actions`), so the climax begins the instant the hunter appears rather than on the quarry's next move. Spawn is **idempotent** (no second hunter in the same room) and recorded on the pursuit via a new `spawned_npc_id` column.
- **What it shipped — the reward loop.** Defeating the hunter is wired through the existing NPC combat-death sweep in `combat_commands.py` (alongside the region-anchor `on_npc_killed_in_combat`): `engine.dsp_hunter_runtime.on_dsp_hunter_killed` reads the `dsp_hunter_for` marker off the dead NPC, **clears the quarry's pursuit** (the trail ends — a fresh pursuit only rebuilds next tick, buying real-time relief), removes the row, and announces the victory to the room. It's a no-op for every non-hunter NPC, so it's cheap to call for each dead combatant. **Prestige-domain: confers no credits** — beating the hunter *is* the reward.
- **What it shipped — reconcile + atonement.** The tick despawns the live hunter when its quarry **atones** (drops under the DSP threshold), and **reconciles escape**: if the quarry slips the hunter (moves rooms), the stale hunter is despawned and the dread resets to `imminent` so it rebuilds toward another climax — a deterministic "got away" handling that needs no separate PC-death hook.
- **Deferred to its own drop (documented, not phantom):** (B) the **communal-rally dark-side-cult villain** — the villain *faction* is decided (dark-side cult, non-player, Q1-clean) but the *rally-objective mechanics* (server-wide threat meter, playerbase coordination, win/lose + rewards) are design-open and deserve a focused pass; and the finer PC-death "hunter collects" consequence beyond the existing death penalty (the spawn+reward+escape-reconcile loop is already complete and playable).
- **Schema:** `dsp_hunter_pursuit` is now schema **42** (added `spawned_npc_id`). Brian's Windows DB runs `MIGRATIONS[42]` on next boot.
- **Handoff:** HANDOFF_decision_clearing_plus_hunter2_drop_2026-06-05.md

## 2026-06-05 — Full Windows suite triage: fix 5 pre-existing failures (none from this session's drops)

- **Context:** The fixed `run_all_tests.bat` ran the full suite on Windows: **6 failed, 7821 passed, 432 skipped, 5 xfailed** in ~10 min. Every one of this session's drops (Drop 3b military procurement, Drop 4b hunter.1, Lane A creatures ×3, the a5_dens robustness tweak) **passed** — none of the 6 failures come from this session's work. The 6 were pre-existing, environmental, or the known deletion residual. Fixed 5; the 6th needs a Windows file deletion.
- **Files:** `tests/spa/test_clickwalk_slugjoin.py`; `tests/test_f7c1_village_trials.py`.
- **Fix 1 — clickwalk slug-join (4 failures): node probe crashed instead of skipping.** `_run_node` guarded node-availability with `subprocess.run(["node","--version"])`, but on a box without node on PATH that call raises `FileNotFoundError` (WinError 2) *before* the returncode can be checked — so the intended `pytest.skip("node not available")` never fired and all four node-logic tests errored. Wrapped the probe in `try/except (FileNotFoundError, OSError) → pytest.skip`. On a machine **with** node the tests run and pass (verified in-sandbox: 6 passed, 1 jsdom-skipped — the production clickwalk logic is correct); on Brian's node-less box they now **skip** cleanly. Pre-existing robustness bug, unrelated to this session.
- **Fix 2 — village NPC count (1 failure): stale hardcoded total.** `test_total_npc_count_includes_all_seven_village` asserted `COUNT(*) FROM npcs == 177`; a clean `build_mos_eisley` produces **196** (verified: 196 rows, **196 distinct names, no duplicates** — all legitimate NPCs, not a duplication bug). The 177 baseline had drifted +19 across intervening content drops that added NPCs without updating this whole-table guard. Bumped to 196 with a documented reconciliation note. **Confirmed in-sandbox the build is identical (196) to the Windows result, so the drift is in committed HEAD — not from this session and not from the creature library (which `build` never loads).** The by-name village-NPC placement checks in the same class (the substantive assertions) were already passing.
- **Verified in-sandbox:** clickwalk → 6 passed / 1 skipped (with node), and the spawn-failure catch confirmed (FileNotFoundError → skip); village count test → 1 passed at 196.
- **Remaining 6th failure (not fixable via a zip overlay):** `test_wow3c_dsp_fp_wiring.py::TestNoLeftoverAdminFpModule::test_admin_fp_module_removed` — still RED because `parser/admin_fp_commands.py` is present on the Windows tree. The E3 consolidation deletes it, but `Expand-Archive` can only add/overwrite, never delete. **Brian must run `Remove-Item parser\admin_fp_commands.py`** (standing residual, re-flagged from the Drop 3b/hunter handoffs).
- **Non-blocking:** the run logged 78 warnings (deprecations; a test-mock `send_json was never awaited` RuntimeWarning in test_session43) — warnings only, not failures, left as-is.
- **Handoff:** HANDOFF_suite_triage_fixes_2026-06-05.md

## 2026-06-05 — Fix: run_all_tests.bat aborts with "ERROR: usage: ... [file_or_dir]"

- **Wave:** Test-infra fix (reported from a Windows run).
- **Files:** `run_all_tests.bat`.
- **Symptom:** `run_all_tests.bat` produced `ERROR: usage: python.exe -m pytest [options] [file_or_dir] ...` and no useful log — the whole suite never ran.
- **Root cause:** the runner unconditionally passed `--timeout=120 --timeout-method=thread`. Those flags only exist when the **pytest-timeout** plugin is installed; without it, pytest rejects the invocation with a usage / `unrecognized arguments` error (reproduced exactly in a clean env). The E3 change added `pytest-timeout>=2.1` to `requirements.txt`, but the runtime env didn't have it installed, so the flags broke the run. (`-o addopts=` already neutralizes `pytest.ini`, so the ini wasn't involved.)
- **Fix:** the runner now **probes** for the plugin (`python -c "import pytest_timeout"`) and adds the `--timeout` flags only when it imports; otherwise it prints a one-line install hint (`pip install pytest-timeout`) and runs **without** the per-test timeout. Either way the suite runs and writes `tests_output.log`. Verified in a clean env: with the plugin absent the flags are dropped and tests run; with it present the flags are passed and accepted.
- **Note:** `run_regression_tests.bat` does **not** pass `--timeout`, so it isn't affected by this bug (it still uses the older Tee-Object redirection, which is a separate, lower-priority robustness item — left unchanged).
- **Recommendation for Brian:** install the plugin to get the hang-protection back — `pip install pytest-timeout` (or `pip install -r requirements.txt`).

---

Wandering the Dune Sea now turns up real creatures (narrative fires today; the live spawn is Phase B).
- **Creature library (`data/npcs_creatures.yaml`, new):** a **standalone generator pool** with WEG D6 stat blocks transcribed from *Creatures of the Galaxy* §2.1 (not invented). Non-intelligent creatures carry **KNO/MEC/TEC = 0D** (faithful, and it stops a future loader defaulting them to 2D). Each entry has the faithful `natural_attack` (tongue / grapple / venomous claws / etc.), plus `armor`, `special`, and `harvest` notes where the source gives them.
- **Two stale-roadmap traps caught before authoring:** (A) the creature file is **deliberately NOT in `era.yaml` content_refs.npcs** — the NPC loader force-places roomless NPCs into `fallback_room_idx` (=8), so a pooled creature library registered there would dump every creature into one room on boot (now guarded by a test); (B) species seeds go in `data/worlds/clone_wars/lore.yaml`, and it was **verified that `seed_lore(era="clone_wars")` loads it at runtime** (`load_era_manifest → load_lore → seed_lore_from_corpus`, and `game_server.py` boots it with `era=get_seeding_era()`) — the "inert at runtime" header comments in both files are themselves stale.

Narrative fires live now; `payload.npc_template` resolves to a creature `id` and is consumed by the Phase B spawner. Dangerous ambush predators (glim worm, stalker lizard) carry a small `min_distance_from_edge` so they appear deeper in the wilds.
- **Lore (`lore.yaml`):** +5 species entries (`category: species` — an open vocabulary, **0 validation errors** so the whole CW lore seed still loads). The worrt text is the extraction doc's; the rest authored faithfully from §2.1.
- **Contract discipline (the heart of the test):** the creature library is the authority for the encounter `npc_template` keys, and the test enforces the contract **in both directions** — every creature encounter's `npc_template` resolves to a real library `id`, **and** every library creature is referenced by at least one live encounter (no orphan creature with no consumer → not a phantom).
- **Tests:** +9 — run against the **real loaders** (`engine.wilderness_loader.load_wilderness_region` + `engine.world_loader.load_lore`), so this is runtime-verified, not byte-grepped: library schema + the KNO/MEC/TEC=0D rule + the force-spawn guard + dune_sea loads with all 5 encounters (narrative present) + the bidirectional encounter↔library contract + lore loads with 0 errors and the 5 species entries present. 9/9 green; all edited YAML re-parsed through the real loaders.
- **Deferred (documented, deliberately NOT shipped as phantom):** (1) **harvest sinks** — `engine/harvest.py`'s `YIELD_TABLE` is keyed `(security_zone, ownership_tier)` (territory resources); there is **no creature-harvest runtime path yet**, so `magus_hide` / hitcher water-sacs live in the creature file's `harvest:` field for when wilderness-harvest ships (§5.7). (2) **Phase B encounter→spawner bridge** — spawn the creature via `create_npc` on a hostile-encounter hit; recommended to **load faithful stats from this library**, not `npc_generator`'s procedural "creature" archetype, so the gathered WEG stats are actually used. (3) **The other biomes** (Kamino / Geonosis / urban vermin / Kuat) + cross-biome hazards + exotic appendix — the same Phase-A pattern, as subsequent increments.

This ships the **roaming-hunter** half's foundation; the live-spawn climax (hunter.2) and the dark-side-cult rally objective remain.
- **Files:** `engine/dsp_hunter.py` (new); `db/database.py` (SCHEMA_VERSION 40→41 + migration 41 + 4 DB methods); `server/tick_handlers_progression.py` (+`dsp_hunter_tick`); `server/game_server.py` (import + register); `engine/bounty_board.py` (notoriety line/section extended); `parser/pc_bounty_commands.py` (passes pursuits map); tests: `tests/test_drop4b_dsp_hunter.py` (+20, new); `tests/test_a5_dens.py` (brittle SCHEMA_VERSION pin made version-robust).
- **What it shipped:** The "soft consequence for the dark path" — once a character's Dark Side Points cross the wanted threshold (DSP 4, the same band the BH board flags), a **named, non-canon bounty hunter** picks up the trail and **closes in over time**. The pursuit escalates through stages (tracking → closing → imminent → at_heels), is surfaced on the BH board under each Marked/Hunted name, and delivers escalating **personal warnings** to the hunted character. The only way to shake it is to **atone** — drop back under the threshold and "the trail goes cold." Deterministic, prestige-domain, faction-agnostic, era/Q1-clean.
- **Engine (`engine/dsp_hunter.py`, pure — no DB/IO):** a 12-name invented Q1-clean roster + deterministic `hunter_for(char_id)` (stable per quarry); `is_wanted` / `should_clear` single-sourced off `bounty_board.DSP_BOUNTY_THRESHOLD` so the hunter and board can't drift; `step_for_dsp` tiered **5 / 9 / 14** by DSP band (the deeper the fall, the faster the hunt); `advance_progress` clamped 0..100; `pursuit_stage`; and the deterministic flavor (`warning_for_stage`, `trail_cold_line`, `fallback_taunt`, `board_suffix`).
- **Persistence:** migration **41** adds `dsp_hunter_pursuit` (`char_id` PK, `hunter_name`, `progress`, `stage`, `last_notified_stage`, `updated_at`) — the *only* persistent state; the "wanted" flag itself stays derived from `dark_side_points` (no bounty rows, no credits). DB API: `get_dsp_pursuit` / `get_all_dsp_pursuits` / `upsert_dsp_pursuit` (a `None` `last_notified_stage` leaves the existing value intact on update) / `clear_dsp_pursuit`.
- **Tick (`dsp_hunter_tick`, mirrors `force_sign_emit_tick`):** advances every wanted PC's pursuit; warns an online + in-game quarry **once per stage change** (the `last_notified_stage` gate, so the held "at your heels" climax doesn't spam); clears pursuits whose quarry has atoned and sends the trail-cold line. Registered at `interval=120, offset=75`. Whole-body and per-PC `try/except` — a bad row never aborts the rest.
- **Board surface:** `format_dsp_notoriety_section(wanted, pursuits=None)` annotates each wanted line with that character's live pursuit suffix (e.g. "— hunter closing"); `format_dsp_notoriety_line` gained an optional `suffix`. The `dsp_hunter` import is **lazy inside the function** to avoid a module-load cycle (dsp_hunter imports bounty_board). `parser/pc_bounty_commands.py` fetches `get_all_dsp_pursuits()` into a map and passes it through (guarded — the section still renders if the fetch fails).
- **Scope discipline (anti-phantom):** v1 is the deterministic **pursuit tracker** — the "actually tracks high-DSP PCs" core — and it has **real consumers** (the board + the warning tick), so it's not a write-with-no-reader. The **live, fightable hunter NPC + reward-on-kill climax** is deferred to a clean, well-scoped **hunter.2**: wiring the spawn + reward into the ~1000-line combat-death block in `parser/combat_commands.py` is the one high-runtime-risk piece, and it isn't rushed into a mega-drop. hunter.2 plan (in the handoff): spawn a fightable hunter NPC at `at_heels` (`db.create_npc` + ai_config `is_dsp_hunter`), idle-Ollama bark via the spawned NPC (`enqueue_bark`, **never Haiku**), reward-on-defeat via the proven `on_npc_killed_in_combat` / anomaly-kill-hook precedent (reads `Combatant.last_attacker_id` + the ai_config tag). (NB `engine/encounter_hunter.py` is a space-side ship pursuit — name-distinct.)
- **Tests:** +20 — pure engine (determinism, era/Q1-clean roster, wanted/clear boundaries, tiered step, clamp + monotonicity, stage boundaries, primary-quarry selection, flavor present); a **real in-memory `Database.initialize()`** test that exercises **migration 41 at runtime** + CRUD incl. the last-notified-intact-on-`None` semantics (guards the byte-pinned-but-not-runtime-pinned trap); tick orchestration via stub DB + sessions (pursuit create + hunter assign, offline-silent-advance, warn-once-per-stage with no repeat, stage-change re-warn, atoned-clear + trail-cold line, non-wanted-never-tracked); and board integration (annotated with pursuits / unannotated without / empty when none). 20/20 green. Adjacent suites re-run green: `test_a5_dens` (18), `test_bounty_board_unit` (23), `test_drop4b_dsp_bounty` (12). All 8 touched files AST-clean.
- **Also:** `test_a5_dens.py::test_v40_migration_present` pinned the literal `"SCHEMA_VERSION = 40"` (would break on any later migration); rewritten to regex the value and assert `>= 40` while still pinning the v40 dens deliverable (mirrors the robust `test_wow1_substrate` pattern).
- **Standing residual (re-flagged):** `parser/admin_fp_commands.py` still needs `Remove-Item parser\admin_fp_commands.py` on Windows (the E3 deletion can't propagate through a zip overlay) — keeps `test_wow3c::test_admin_fp_module_removed` RED. Pre-existing, unrelated to this drop.
- **Handoff:** HANDOFF_drop4b_dsp_hunter_2026-06-05.md

## 2026-06-05 — Drop 3b: military ship procurement (faction-gated warships)

- **Wave:** Audit remediation / Drop 3 capital sinks (`T2.ECON.trade_remap_and_sinks`). Closes the `3b_military_procurement` gap; with it, Drop 3's required sink work is complete (only optional additive depth, `3b_3c`, remains).
- **Files:** `parser/shipyard_commands.py`; tests: `tests/test_drop3b_military_procurement.py` (+33, new).
- **What it shipped:** A faction-gated military requisition channel alongside the Drop 3a civilian brokerage. New command `+warship` (aliases `warship` / `+shipreq` / `+procure` / `+commission` — collision-checked against commissary's `+requisition`): no-args lists the war-materiel catalog annotated with per-viewer ✓/✗ eligibility and a "Requires:" line; `+warship requisition <hull> [name]` (also `req` / `buy`) requisitions a hull. Eligibility is **faction membership + rank**, not a broker location, so a member draws materiel through their own chain of command and it's delivered to a staging pad. A civilian still cannot buy a gunship.
- **Catalog (gates):** CIS — `vulture_droid` (cis rank 1), `hyena_bomber` (cis 2), `tri_fighter` (cis 2); Republic — `v_19_torrent` (republic 1), `arc_170` (republic 2), `laat_gunship` (republic 3); and `eta_2_actis` dual-gated `{republic: 3, jedi_order: 1}` (the iconic Jedi interceptor, open to Knights as well as senior Republic aces). Prices are single-sourced from `ShipTemplate.cost` (same discipline as 3a — a hull that doesn't resolve or lacks a cost is dropped with a loud log line, never sold at a bogus price).
- **Refactor (single money-path):** extracted `_finalize_ship_purchase(...)` (debit-first through `adjust_credits` → bridge room → ship insert → owned-flag → disembark exit, **refund-safe** via `f"{source_tag}_refund"`) from `purchase_ship`'s tail. Both the civilian brokerage and the military requisition call it; they differ only in eligibility gate, ledger tag, and interior flavor. The civilian path is byte-for-byte behaviourally unchanged (tag `ship_purchase`, dock-resolved-before-debit ordering intact) — verified by the unchanged 20/20 Drop 3a suite.
- **Ledger:** military spend sinks as `adjust_credits(..., "ship_requisition")` (refund `ship_requisition_refund`) — a **distinct** source from the civilian `ship_purchase`, so it surfaces separately on `@economy`. All credit movement stays on the ledger chokepoint.
- **Helpers:** `build_military_catalog()`; `_member_rank(db, char, faction_code)` (fail-soft → `None` = non-member, never raises into the flow); `_rank_title(db, faction_code, level)` (→ `"rank N"` fallback); `requisition_ship(...)` (location-agnostic — `room_id` accepted for future gating). `register_shipyard_commands` now registers both `ShipyardCommand` and `WarshipCommand`.
- **Tunable first-cuts (flagged for Brian):** the per-hull rank floors; Eta-2 being open to Jedi rank 1; and requisition being location-agnostic (a faction-HQ location gate + faction-specific hangar delivery is an easy follow-up if more friction is wanted).
- **Tests:** +33 — catalog shape / exact gates / CIS–Republic split / era-cleanness / prices-single-sourced; `_member_rank` (member / base-rank-0 / non-member / unresolved-org / garbage-rank→0); the full requisition gate matrix (wrong faction, independent, stale-faction_id-no-membership, rank-too-low, exact-rank success, above-rank success, the Eta-2 dual gate at Jedi 0/1 and Republic 2/3, broke, ownership cap, no-dock, refund-on-insert-failure tagging `ship_requisition`/`ship_requisition_refund`, custom name, unknown hull) with **every rejection charging nothing**; cross-catalog isolation both directions; `WarshipCommand` key/aliases, register-both, catalog-view-charges-nothing, and end-to-end requisition execute. Civilian Drop 3a suite re-run **20/20 green** (refactor regression-free).
- **Handoff:** HANDOFF_drop3b_military_procurement_2026-06-05.md

## 2026-06-04 — Drop 0a tail: patrol encounter B3 era-cleanness

- **Wave:** B3 era-cleanness (standing quality regime). Same session as 4a/4a.2/4b; folded into the rollup.
- **Files:** `engine/encounter_patrol.py`; tests: `tests/test_drop0a_patrol_era_cleanness.py` (+5, new).
- **The leak:** the space patrol encounter was broadcasting hardcoded Empire-era strings to players in the Clone Wars production era — `[IMPERIAL BOARDING] Stormtroopers board for inspection.`, `[IMPERIAL CUSTOMS] …`, `[IMPERIAL CUSTOMS] You are being detained.`, `[IMPERIAL BOARDING] Troops withdraw.` (in `_apply_infraction`), and `[INSPECTION] Stormtroopers inspect the hold …` (in the clean-inspection branch). A literal Imperial boarding party in a ~20 BBY game — a B3 violation.
- **The fix:** all five player-facing strings now route through the module's existing **authority-aware** label helpers (`_default_patrol_name` / `_board_party`, keyed off the zone's controlling faction → Republic / CIS / Hutt / neutral), so a Republic-controlled zone reads "[Republic Sector Patrol] Clone troopers board for inspection.", a Hutt zone reads "Hutt Cartel Customs / Cartel enforcers", etc. `_apply_infraction` reuses the `patrol_name` already cached in `encounter.context` (same pattern as the rest of the encounter). Docstrings/comments mentioning "Imperial" were also cleaned (header, the security comment, the registration docstring); the only remaining "Imperial" mentions are design comments explaining the era-aware approach.
- **Tests (sandbox, changed-module only — Windows full pytest is ground truth):** `test_drop0a_patrol_era_cleanness` **5 passed** (the label tables carry no Empire-era tokens and map republic→Clone troopers / cis→B1 battle droids; `_apply_infraction` broadcasts contain no Imperial/Stormtrooper for the fine, detained, and Hutt-authority paths, and carry the era-appropriate authority + party). Regression: `test_session46_encounter_dispatch` + `test_session57b_space_umbrellas` + `test_kd5b_sweep_npc_space_traffic` **84 passed** with the new test. AST-clean. No JS touched.
- **Resolves:** the long-standing "`encounter_patrol` B3 leak (`_apply_infraction` hardcodes Imperial strings)" open item.

## 2026-06-04 — Drop 4b (partial): Dark-Side Notoriety — auto-DSP bounty

- **Wave:** Audit remediation / "fun additions" — the III.3 communal half, decision (c). Same session as 4a/4a.2. **This is the well-specified, contained slice of 4b**; the roaming-hunter NPC, the reward-on-kill loop, and the communal-rally villain are tracked as follow-on (see "Deferred / decisions" below).
- **Files:** `engine/bounty_board.py`, `db/database.py`, `parser/force_commands.py`, `parser/pc_bounty_commands.py`; tests: `tests/test_drop4b_dsp_bounty.py` (+12, new).
- **What it shipped — the auto-DSP-bounty trigger + board surface, DSP-DERIVED (no schema change):** a high-DSP character automatically draws a bounty. Per decision (c) this is **deterministic, no new AI cost, faction-agnostic** (it tracks the dark side, not a player faction), and the reward is **status / prestige only** — it never touches the credit / insurance / claim flow of the `pc_bounties` system. The "wanted" state is computed from `dark_side_points` the way `force_sensitive` is derived from the Force attributes; **no new table, no migration.**
  - `engine/bounty_board.py` — `DSP_BOUNTY_THRESHOLD = 4` (the forcestatus "Danger Zone" band), `is_dsp_wanted`, `crossed_into_wanted` (fires the notice exactly once on the first crossing), `dsp_bounty_tier` (Marked / Hunted / Darkest of the Dark), `format_dsp_notoriety_line` / `format_dsp_notoriety_section` (prestige-labelled, no credits).
  - `db/database.py` — `get_dsp_wanted_characters(threshold, limit)`: read-only `SELECT … FROM characters WHERE dark_side_points >= ? AND is_active = 1 ORDER BY dark_side_points DESC`. No rows are written.
  - `parser/force_commands.py` — `ForceCommand.execute` snapshots DSP before the power resolves and, on a first crossing into wanted, sends a one-time `[BOUNTY]` notice (faction-agnostic, prestige-only). Deterministic; optional idle-Ollama flavor is a documented seam (NOT shipped, NEVER Haiku).
  - `parser/pc_bounty_commands.py` — the BH-Guild board (`_handle_board`) appends a **Dark-Side Notoriety** section listing DSP-wanted PCs (prestige reward); the board now renders even when there are no credit bounties but there is notoriety.
- **Tests (sandbox, changed-module only — Windows full pytest is ground truth):** `test_drop4b_dsp_bounty` **12 passed** (threshold/wanted, crossing-fires-once incl. the already-wanted and not-increasing cases, tier labels, section filter+sort+prestige-not-credits, the `get_dsp_wanted_characters` param binding + dict rows via a recording stand-in, the crossing notice through `ForceCommand.execute` with resolve patched [fires on 3→4, silent on 4→5 and on a no-DSP power], and the BH board surface [shows notoriety for a Guild member, refuses a non-member]). Regression on touched neighbours: `test_bounty_board_unit` **23 passed**, `test_pg2_pc_bounty_session1/2` **78 passed** (PvP credit-bounty + insurance flow untouched), force drop modules **58 passed**. All 12 session-touched `.py` files AST-clean. No JS touched.
- **Deferred / decisions for Brian (the rest of III.3):**
  - **The roaming-hunter NPC** (a persistent antagonist that pursues the marked PC) and the **reward-on-kill loop** (awarding prestige to whoever brings a marked PC down) are larger — they touch NPC spawning/movement and the combat-death hook. Designed-but-not-built here; recommend a dedicated follow-on drop.
  - **The communal-rally villain** (other half of III.3) is explicitly **"decide at 4b"** — it needs a **non-player faction** (CIS≈Geonosian and Hutt are both player factions and were rejected). **Recommendation:** a **dark-side cult** (e.g., a fledgling Nightsister-adjacent or fallen-Force splinter, era-clean, no canonical names) — it ties thematically to the DSP-notoriety system shipped here and gives "rally against a common darkness" coherence with the Jedi-village/Force content. Alternatives: rogue/reprogrammed droid swarm, or a great-beast threat. Awaiting your pick before building the rally objective.
- **Handoff:** `HANDOFF_drop_4b_dsp_bounty_2026-06-04.md`. This delivery is a combined **4a + 4a.2 + 4b** rollup.

## 2026-06-04 — Drop 4a.2: telepathy + sense-lie + farseeing + danger-sense

- **Wave:** Audit remediation / "fun additions" (T1.3.2). Stacks on Drop 4a's effect-application substrate (same session). Four further **Sense** powers, all light (`dark_side=False`).
- **Files:** `engine/force_powers.py`, `engine/combat.py`, `parser/force_commands.py`; tests: `tests/test_drop4a2_sense_powers.py` (+20, new), `tests/test_force_powers_unit.py` (power-count assertion 9 → 13).
- **New powers** (POWERS count 9 → **13**):
  - **telepathy** (Sense, MODERATE) — between two **PCs sharing an active Master-Padawan bond** (read from the `master_padawan_bond` table via `get_active_bond_for_padawan`) it is a deep communion across distance and reports the partner's wound/condition; otherwise a wordless mind-touch **offered** to the other player to RP; against an NPC it skims surface thoughts (reuses the 4a pry read). It does **not** create bonds — it uses the formal P-M system.
  - **sense_lie** "Sense Deception" (Sense, MODERATE) — reveals whether an NPC is concealing something (reads real `lying`/`deceptive`/`secret`/`true_intent`/`motive` flags, consistent with the 4a data model) and may surface what; an honest NPC reads as truthful; a **PC** target is offered the read.
  - **farseeing** (Sense, DIFFICULT) — a simple portent tied to **real nearby danger** (a hostile NPC in the room yields a warning vision; otherwise a calm portent). Rich, scripted visions remain tracked for **G5**.
  - **danger_sense** (Sense, MODERATE) — in combat, a **one-shot initiative reroll keeping the better result**; out of combat, an early warning.
- **Combat engine:** `Combatant` gains `initiative_reroll: bool = False` (default off → no behavior change); `CombatInstance.roll_initiative` honors it by rolling twice and keeping the higher total, then consuming the flag. `danger_sense` sets the flag on the caster's live combatant via `combat_commands._ensure_in_combat` (the established parser→combat accessor).
- **Parser:** new appliers `_apply_telepathy`, `_apply_sense_lie`, `_apply_farseeing`, `_apply_danger_sense` dispatched from `_apply_force_effects`; `_npc_is_hostile` helper for farseeing; room-broadcast templates for all four. telepathy/sense_lie route through the 4a NPC/PC target resolution and the offered-effect path; farseeing/danger_sense are self-targeted.
- **Tests (sandbox, changed-module only — Windows full pytest is ground truth):** `test_drop4a2_sense_powers` **20 passed** (4 powers present + light, count 13, resolver effect_kind signals; initiative reroll **keeps the better** of two patched rolls + consumes the flag + leaves a single roll when off; bonded-PC communion + partner notify, unbonded-PC offered, NPC surface-thought; deceit revealed vs honest-reads-clean vs PC-offered; danger/calm portent; danger_sense sets the combat reroll flag / out-of-combat warning). `test_combat_mechanics` **31 passed** (roll_initiative regression). `test_force_powers_unit` **38 passed** (count bumped to 13). All 8 touched `.py` files AST-clean. No JS touched.
- **Handoff:** `HANDOFF_drop_4a2_sense_powers_2026-06-04.md` (and `HANDOFF_drop_4a_social_force_2026-06-04.md` — this delivery is a combined 4a + 4a.2 rollup).

## 2026-06-04 — Drop 4a: social-Force mechanical teeth + mind-trick split

- **Wave:** Audit remediation / "fun additions" (T1.3). Built on the E3-green baseline. Implements the Part V / Drop 4 locked decision set (TODO.json `design_calls_resolved_recent`, 2026-06-04): the previously **narrative-only** social/sense/alter powers now change real game state, and the Jedi mind trick is split out of the dark side.
- **Files:** `engine/force_powers.py`, `engine/buffs.py`, `engine/city_guard_runtime.py`, `parser/force_commands.py`; tests: `tests/test_drop4a_social_force.py` (+26, new), `tests/test_force_powers_unit.py` (2 stale assertions updated for the split).
- **Mind-trick SPLIT:** `affect_mind` is now the **light suggestion** — `dark_side=False`, **no DSP** (was `dark_side=True`). A new `dominate_mind` (coercion, base_diff DIFFICULT) carries the dark side: `dark_side=True`, auto-DSP. The existing `power.dark_side`→DSP machinery drives both, so the split is a flag move plus one new POWERS entry. Power count 8 → **9**.
- **WEG-faithful opposed roll (corrected mid-build):** against an NPC, mind influence is resolved as a real **opposed willpower roll** — the target resists with willpower (untrained → its governing attribute, so a weak-minded being resists poorly and is easily swayed), and the base complexity is a floor: `difficulty = max(base_diff, resist_roll)`. The earlier draft used the NPC's willpower as a flat difficulty; that was changed to an actual roll. "Deterministic" (per the locked decision) means the **engine** rolls it with no human-target turn — not that it is a fixed number. Mirrors the module's existing `injure_kill` opposed-resistance pattern. For a **PC** target no resistance is rolled (the engine never auto-rolls another player's mind); the difficulty stays the base complexity and the parser **offers** the formed suggestion.
- **Real teeth on the four narrative-only powers** (engine records `effect_kind` + payload; the parser, which owns DB/room context, applies it):
  - `affect_mind` / `dominate_mind` on an **NPC**: a **city guard** → the caster gains the time-boxed `mind_trick_unseen` buff (new flag-only `BUFF_TEMPLATES` entry, 5 min), consumed by `city_guard_runtime.should_city_guard_engage` which now returns False for a buffed character ("you don't need to see his identification"). A **generic NPC** → **pry-info**, revealing a real hidden fact from the NPC's sheet/AI-config (`secret`/`knows`/`true_intent`/`motive`/`disposition`, falling back to description). A command (domination) pries harder/truer.
  - `affect_mind` / `dominate_mind` on a **PC**: **offered effect** — the target player is sent the nudge to RP; their character is **never** mechanically mutated. (DSP for domination still accrues to the caster — using coercion is dark regardless of compliance.)
  - `telekinesis` vs a target with margin ≥ 3 → **real disarm** (parser clears the target's equipped weapon and persists: PC via the `equipment` column, NPC via `char_sheet_json`); below the margin it only shoves.
  - `life_sense` → enumerates the **real** living beings in the room (PCs + NPCs, self excluded); `sense_force` → reports the **real** Force-sensitive and dark-tinged beings present.
- **Parser:** `force <power> <target>` now resolves **NPC** targets in the room (guards, merchants, bystanders) in addition to PCs, via the canonical `npc_combat_ai.build_npc_character` so opposed rolls and disarm read the NPC's real sheet. `dominate_mind` added to the room-broadcast templates. `force_sensitive` stays a **derived** state (never a `save_character` kwarg).
- **Deferred, with rationale (NOT shipped):** `affect_mind` → **vendor-price** has no single clean consumer — `skill_checks.resolve_bargain_check` bypasses `perform_skill_check`/buffs, and NPC-vendor bargaining is "scattered across ≥4 places / deferred" (per `player_cities.py`). Wiring it would touch multiple fragile sites; folded into a later drop rather than shipped as a write-with-no-reader phantom. **Drop 4a.2** (telepathy/Master-Padawan bond, farseeing/danger-sense + simple vision, sense-lie) is the next session. **Note on rolls:** force-power rolls continue through `force_powers`' own canonical roll path (the established WoW.3c-integrated path on `control/sense/alter` pools), not `perform_skill_check` (which is built around `skills.yaml` skills on char dicts); no new ad-hoc rolls were introduced. Flagged for Brian in the handoff.
- **Tests (sandbox, changed-module only — full suite is Brian's Windows ground truth):** `test_drop4a_social_force` **26 passed** (split, no-DSP, opposed-difficulty invariant, disarm margin-gate, real sense enumeration, guard-pacify buff + persist, generic pry, PC offered-not-applied, PC/NPC disarm persistence, guard-engage short-circuit, end-to-end execute wiring). `test_force_powers_unit` **38 passed** after updating the two stale assertions (`len(POWERS)` 8→9; dark set `{injure_kill, affect_mind}`→`{injure_kill, dominate_mind}`). Regression on touched neighbours: `test_cities_phase7_guards` + `test_cities_phase7c_combat` **73 passed**; buff consumers (`test_srb1_medic_stim`, `test_srb1b_stim_consumable_wiring`, `test_code_review_d5_json_loads_narrowing`) **72 passed**. All 6 touched `.py` files AST-clean. No JS touched.
- **Orthogonal:** `parser/admin_fp_commands.py` is still present in the tree (the E3 manual `del` was not applied), so `test_wow3c::test_admin_fp_module_removed` stays RED until deleted — unrelated to 4a.
- **Handoff:** `HANDOFF_drop_4a_social_force_2026-06-04.md`

## 2026-06-04 — E3: red-board remediation (full-suite test health)

- **Wave:** Audit remediation (post-Drop 3 / post-E2). Standalone test-health drop. **No production behaviour changes** beyond two silent-except → `log.debug` lint fixes and the removal of one already-orphaned module; everything else is test/tooling. Greens the board so Drop 4a (social-Force mechanics) builds on a clean baseline.
- **Trigger:** Windows ground-truth full run reported **23 failed / 7701 passed / 428 skipped** (656s). Each failure root-caused; classified as stale-test (code moved, test didn't), test-harness gap, production lint, environmental (sandbox-vs-Windows), or conscious-tripwire.
- **Result:** **18 of 23 fixed and verified green in the Linux sandbox** (changed-module runs). 4 are environmental (Windows-node), 1 is a tripwire left RED pending Brian's confirm-then-bump. One *additional* seedless-statistical flake surfaced during verification (not in the 23) and is flagged, untouched.
- **Fixes — stale assertions (test lagged intended balance/state; code is correct, test caught up):**
  - `test_skill_checks_unit::test_partial_success_pays_fraction` — Audit v2 §2.1 tightened the partial window to `margin ≥ -2` and the fraction to `0.40`; dice `[3,3,2]→[3,4,2]` (margin -3→-2) and expected `375→200` (0.40×500). (Already documented as a known stale test in the E2 entry.)
  - `tests/smoke/scenarios/pc_bounty_session2.py` (BTY-6) — Drop 2 rescaled the death-insurance hit to **flat + %** (`engine/death.py`: `INSURANCE_FLAT=250` + `INSURANCE_PCT=10`); a 10 000-cr bounty now costs the target **1 250** (250 + 1 000), not 1 000. Assertion + comment updated; the 8 000-cr (80%) BH-payout assertion left intact (still correct).
  - `test_market_state_persistence` (`== "SCHEMA_VERSION = 38"` → robust parse + `>= 38`), `test_wow1_substrate` (`SCHEMA_VERSION == 35` → `>= 35`) — schema is at v40; these now pin "at least the migration that introduced the feature" rather than an exact frozen number.
  - `test_session58_cleanup_umbrellas` — Drop 3 added `prestige`; expected `_HOME_SWITCH_IMPL` keys now `{view, sethome, admin, prestige}`.
  - `test_wow3c_dsp_fp_wiring::test_admin_fp_module_removed` — the assertion was correct; the module just hadn't been deleted (see below).
- **Fixes — test-harness / fake-DB gaps (Drop 1 ledger migration missed these fakes):**
  - `adjust_credits` shim added to four stale test fakes whose real call sites were migrated to the metered chokepoint: `test_syn5_espionage_as_influence`, `test_syn7a_wilderness_anomalies`, `test_syn7b_wilderness_anomalies_tier2` (sqlite-backed `_MiniDB`, via `self._db.execute`; `char_id==0 → return 0`), and `test_cities_phase6_maintenance` `_FakeDB` (dict-backed; `city_tax` routes through `adjust_credits(0, -take, "city_tax")`). `test_syn7a` additionally never seeded its char row, so the migrated `UPDATE characters` path had nothing to update — added the `INSERT INTO characters` (syn5/syn7b already seeded theirs).

Added `engine.player_cities.ensure_schema(srv.db)` mirroring `server/game_server.py`. This is what was breaking BTY-6's setup.
- **Fix — real test-ordering bug (not stale):** `test_poi_feed` had **two** raw `engine.bounty_board.get_bounty_board = …` monkeypatches with no restore. The second permanently replaced the real getter with a fake lambda, so `test_singleton_bindings[bounty_board]` (which asserts `GameServer.bounty_board is get_bounty_board()`) failed whenever poi_feed ran first. Converted both to the auto-restoring `monkeypatch` fixture (matching the rest of the file). singleton_bindings now passes regardless of order. *(An earlier try/finally patch on only the second site was insufficient — it captured the lambda the first site had already leaked; the fix had to address the upstream site.)*
- **Fix — production lint (the only production-code touch):** two `except Exception: … pass` blocks flagged by `test_session38::test_no_silent_except_pass_in_production` → `log.debug(..., exc_info=True)`: `engine/titles.py` and `parser/bounty_commands.py` (the E2 bounty-surge block).

- **Fix — optional-dependency guard:** the two `make_substrate_seed.py` loader tests (`test_wilderness_substrate_seed`, `test_wilderness_overview_faithful`) errored with `ModuleNotFoundError: PIL` on Brian's box (no Pillow). Added `pytest.importorskip("PIL", …)` inside `_load_tool`, gated to the substrate tool, so they **skip** cleanly without Pillow and **run** when it's installed (sandbox: 28 passed). Pillow can be `pip install`'d if Brian wants those map tests to actually execute rather than skip.
- **Fix — fragile-window test:** `test_bearing_wireup::test_move_command_records_bearing` sliced `src[start:start+3000]` to assert the bearing wiring; the move hook grew past 3 000 chars so the slice missed the (present, correct) wiring. Replaced with a slice bounded by the next `def`/`async def`; the single `save_character(..., attributes=…)` occurrence keeps the `count == 1` assertion exact.
- **Environmental — REPORTED, no code change:** `tests/spa/test_clickwalk_slugjoin.py` ×4 — **pass in the Linux sandbox** (node v22.22.2: 6 passed, 1 skipped) and already skip when node is absent. Brian's Windows box has node but produces a different result; need `proc.stderr` from his box (likely a node-version or Windows subprocess/newline/temp-file quirk).
- **Tripwire — FLAGGED, left RED:** `test_f7c1_village_trials::test_total_npc_count_includes_all_seven_village` asserts `COUNT(*) FROM npcs == 177`; actual is **196** (+19 from recent drops: e.g. Senator Iolanthe Kress, Independent Trader Sela Dorne, Kabe). This is a deliberate conscious-review canary — **not** auto-bumped. Recommendation: confirm the 19 additions are intended (no dupes / Q1 violations), then either bump 177→196 or refactor to assert the seven village NPCs by name (robust).
- **Flagged flake (NOT in the 23):** `test_session38::TestTextureEncounterTick::test_security_scaling` — seedless statistical test (5 000 iters, real `random`, conftest doesn't seed). Passed in Brian's full run; coin-flipped in the isolated sandbox run (lawless=24 vs secured=32). Both counts ≈0.5% suggests the secured/lawless multiplier isn't separating in an isolated run (the zone→security lookup likely needs world/registry data the full suite has loaded). Zero causal link to E3. Left untouched; recommend hardening later (mock `random` like the sibling `test_trigger_during_hyperspace` does, or assert on probability with a fixed seed).
- **Tooling — `run_all_tests.bat` hang + no log:** the old PowerShell `Tee-Object` buffered output and lost the log on Ctrl+C, and a hanging test stalled the run forever. Rewrote to plain `> tests_output.log 2>&1` redirection (survives Ctrl+C) + `--timeout=120 --timeout-method=thread` (kills a hanging test so the run finishes and the log writes) + `--continue-on-collection-errors --maxfail=999 -o addopts= -q`. Added `pytest-timeout>=2.1` to `requirements.txt` (run `pip install -r requirements.txt` before the next batch run).

## 2026-06-04 — E2: wire the dormant world-event PASSIVE effects (+ phantom repair)

- **Wave:** Audit remediation (post-Drop 3). Rolled up with E1 in the same combined zip. Wires the *passive* subset of the dormant world-event `mechanical_effects` to their existing faucets (the proven `get_effect()` pattern), and **repairs a phantom**: `patrol_spawn_mult` was never actually consumed.
- **Scope decision:** E2 = only the **passive** effects (scale/modify an existing mechanic at an existing faucet, **no new player interaction**). The 6 **flag** effects each *enable a new interaction* and need a design decision, so per the design/implementation-separation discipline they were split out to a design pass (`T2.E3.flag_event_interactions_design`): `contraband_scan`, `rare_vendor`, `hutt_auction`/`criminal_rep_gate`, `krayt_bounty`, `brawl_active`, `distress_active`.
- **Wired (authoritative effect keys from `EVENT_DEFS`):**
  - `bounty_reward_mult` (BOUNTY_SURGE, ×2) → `parser/bounty_commands.py`: read `get_effect("bounty_reward_mult", 1.0)` and scale `reward` **before** the metered `adjust_credits(..., "bounty")` payout; surfaces a "bounty surge … pays N credits extra" line. No-op (1.0) when inactive.
  - `pirate_spawn_mult` (PIRATE_SURGE, ×3) **and** `patrol_spawn_mult` (SECURITY_CRACKDOWN, ×2) → `engine/npc_space_traffic.py::_pick_archetype` spawn weighting.
  - `perception_penalty` (SANDSTORM, −3 pips = −1D) → `engine/skill_checks.py::perform_skill_check`, folded into the central pip-modifier slot but **guarded to the observation-skill family** `{perception, search}` (new `_ENV_PERCEPTION_SKILLS`) so it never touches the many social skills that merely fall back to the PERCEPTION attribute. No-op (default 0) when inactive — transparent to the suite and to every non-observation check; the only path here that reaches the world-event singleton.
- **PHANTOM REPAIRED (`patrol_spawn_mult`):** `npc_space_traffic.py` had **two** `_pick_archetype` definitions — a world-event-aware one **shadowed** by a later `_pick_archetype(exclude_hunter=True)` (the one `_spawn` actually calls). So `patrol_spawn_mult` (long claimed "live") had **never** been consumed at runtime, and no test caught it (the E1 test only asserts the effect is *declared* on the event). Fix: deleted the dead duplicate and consolidated **both** multipliers into the live definition (each `max(0, int(weight*mult))`, with a `total<=0 → TRADER` guard). Proven live by consumption tests — patrol share **0.158→0.298** under SECURITY_CRACKDOWN, pirate **0.173→0.378** under PIRATE_SURGE.
- **Bookkeeping in the same drop:** Director LLM event vocab `EVENT_TYPES` += `intelligence_thaw`, `spice_demand` (closes `TD.DIRECTOR_EVENT_VOCAB_GAP` — they previously only auto-fired on the timer). Live "Jabba" Q1 named-figure strings cleaned → `HUTT_AUCTION` announce ("A Hutt kajidic is running an auction") and `_ZONE_DISPLAY_NAMES["jabba"]` ("the Hutt quarter").
- **Files:** `engine/world_events.py`, `engine/skill_checks.py`, `engine/npc_space_traffic.py`, `engine/director.py`, `parser/bounty_commands.py`, `tests/test_e2_dormant_effects.py` (NEW).
- **Tests:** +9 — `tests/test_e2_dormant_effects.py` (DB-free; a `clean_events` fixture snapshots/clears/restores the world-event singleton and injects `ActiveEvent` directly to bypass `activate_event`'s global cooldown). **Consumption** tests (pirate skew, patrol skew, sandstorm drops the observation pool 5D→4D, sandstorm no-op on a non-observation skill, no-event no-op) + **structural** pins (exactly one `_pick_archetype` def — shadow regression guard; `bounty_reward_mult` read precedes the payout; Director vocab has the two new events; no "Jabba" in any EventDef string or zone-display value).
- **Regression (sandbox, changed modules):** no E2-caused failures; `test_srb3_combined_action` (the lead-bonus suite that shares the exact `perform_skill_check` block edited here) **passes**. **Two PRE-EXISTING / ENVIRONMENTAL failures observed and confirmed NOT caused by E2:** `test_skill_checks_unit::TestResolveMissionCompletion::test_partial_success_pays_fraction` (a stale test — `MISSION_SKILL_MAP["investigation"]` fraction has drifted to `0.40`; **proven to fail identically on reverted, baseline-equivalent code**), and `test_srb2_morale_aura` (37 failures — a DB+asyncio harness that can't run in the bare sandbox, like the aiohttp-dependent `test_singleton_bindings`). Both are for the Windows ground-truth run to confirm.
- **Smoke (Windows):** the `perform_skill_check` change is the one touch to a high-blast-radius central function — trigger/admin-activate `sandstorm` and confirm a `search`/`perception` check drops by 1D while a `blaster`/social check is unchanged; activate `bounty_surge` and collect a bounty (payout ×2 + surge line); activate `pirate_surge`/`security_crackdown` and confirm traffic skews.
- **Handoff:** `HANDOFF_e2_dormant_effects_2026-06-04.md`
